  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e0f53a50-56ed-4f78-9dc5-5f0358ec8aa8'
      });
    }

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/103567089-philipandarihanna-ransom">PhilipandArihanna Ransom</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I thought it was perfectly find for a middle schooler, but it depends on what you mean by "sexual content". She learns how babies are made, but she do<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I thought it was perfectly find for a middle schooler, but it depends on what you mean by "sexual content". She learns how babies are made, but she doesn't engage in sexual activity...she's 10. It is more a book about coming of age, and addresses some big topics, like racial segregation in the Southern United States in the 1940s. She does end up kissing a boy though, so like I said, it really depends on what you think is appropriate for YOUR CHILD, (or yourself, I suppose).<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9145671" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/419287-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1289534648p2/419287.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/9145671?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/419287-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone with a tenuous grip on reality</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/419287-jessica?shelf=wee-ones-and-bored-teenagers">wee-ones-and-bored-teenagers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9145671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6533587642534483890">I thought about giving this a five, and it might deserve one.<br/><br/>This is Judy Blume's best book. It's written for a younger crowd than her Puberty books, and Sally's concerns lie in the elementary school horrors of shame and embarrassment and trying to fit in. These are conveyed spectacularly well, as when she discovers upon moving to Florida that there are no doors on the bathroom stalls at her new school. Imagine!! The details in this book -- the social necessity of not wearing socks, the way the </span>
  <span id="freeText6533587642534483890" style="display:none">I thought about giving this a five, and it might deserve one.<br /><br />This is Judy Blume's best book. It's written for a younger crowd than her Puberty books, and Sally's concerns lie in the elementary school horrors of shame and embarrassment and trying to fit in. These are conveyed spectacularly well, as when she discovers upon moving to Florida that there are no doors on the bathroom stalls at her new school. Imagine!! The details in this book -- the social necessity of not wearing socks, the way the grass is different in Florida than New Jersey (NJ?) -- totally stuck with me, probably because I reread this book multiple times.<br /><br />But what makes this book spectacular instead of just another kid-issue book is Sally J. Freedman's bizarre, vivid fantasy life, documented in riveting italic sections. The way Sally uses her family's actual experience of the Holocaust as melodramatic fodder for her imagination is dead brilliant: that's exactly the kind of thing kids do! Sally's fantasies were very entertaining, in part because they were so appropriately inappropriate, and were the reason I kept returning to this book. This book provoked a desire to watch an Esther Williams movie, which I have never got around to fulfilling.<br /><br />I wonder if it's as great as I remember it.... did anyone else here like this one?</span>
  <a data-text-id="6533587642534483890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_7284707" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/7284707" />
    <a title="Presley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/468484-presley"><img alt="Presley" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/7284707?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Presley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Presley" href="/user/show/468484-presley">Presley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer7284707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11522226223701615223">"Starring Sally J. Freedman as Herself" is my favorite book. It's about ten-year-old Sally who moves to Maimi Beach for the winter since her brother has a kidney infection and needs to stay in warmth. The book takes place in the post World War Two era. The book doesn't really have a main conflict, but you see Sally encounter world conflicts through naive eyes. She questions segregation a lot and she gets the same answers from adults: That's just the way things are. You also see Sally encounter e</span>
  <span id="freeText11522226223701615223" style="display:none">"Starring Sally J. Freedman as Herself" is my favorite book. It's about ten-year-old Sally who moves to Maimi Beach for the winter since her brother has a kidney infection and needs to stay in warmth. The book takes place in the post World War Two era. The book doesn't really have a main conflict, but you see Sally encounter world conflicts through naive eyes. She questions segregation a lot and she gets the same answers from adults: That's just the way things are. You also see Sally encounter everyday obstacles that continue today: sibling rivalry, problems with bullies, friendship jealousy, etc. That is probably my favorite thing about this book: it doesn't have some unrealistic main problem that the book is all about. It deals with small problems everyone has. I also like that it takes place in another time, to show that some things never change and to show the similarities between two very different times.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11522226223701615223" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2248975393" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2248975393" />
    <a title="Manybooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks"><img alt="Manybooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459773375p2/2970379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2248975393?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manybooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manybooks" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks">Manybooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=national-socialism">national-socialism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=judy-blume">judy-blume</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=biographies-memoirs">biographies-memoirs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=painful">painful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2248975393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13585508412416253569">I know that <u>Starring Sally J. Freedman as Herself</u> supposedly is very much autobiographical in scope, and with this salient truth in mind, I do to a certain point very much applaud Judy Blume for not in any way sugar-coating or attempting to make light of the fact that once Sally (who is obviously based on the author herself), her mother and ailing older brother have moved to Florida (because of Douglas' nephritis), she absolutely despises her elderly neighbour Mr. Zavodsky and actually believes </span>
  <span id="freeText13585508412416253569" style="display:none">I know that <u>Starring Sally J. Freedman as Herself</u> supposedly is very much autobiographical in scope, and with this salient truth in mind, I do to a certain point very much applaud Judy Blume for not in any way sugar-coating or attempting to make light of the fact that once Sally (who is obviously based on the author herself), her mother and ailing older brother have moved to Florida (because of Douglas' nephritis), she absolutely despises her elderly neighbour Mr. Zavodsky and actually believes he is Adolf Hitler in disguise simply because of his Central European looks and likely heavy foreign accent (and even writes many poison-pen accusatory letters to him, which she fortunately does not mail). <br /><br />But the above all having been said, and even though I am now as an older adult able to at least somewhat appreciate Judy Blume's honesty and candour, I do have to admit that I absolutely and totally hated (with every fibre of my being at that) <u>Starring Sally J. Freedman as Herself</u> when I read this novel in 1977, in grade five, as a brand new hardcover library book (and only one year after our family's immigration to Canada from Germany, at the absolute height of me being constantly bullied and harassed by both students and even some of my teachers due to my German background and because I spoke English with a rather heavy accent). In fact, I despised <u>Starring Sally J. Freedman as Herself</u> to such an extent I even ended up writing a letter to Judy Blume, an emotional epistle accusing her of using pretty much the same rhetoric regarding ALL Germans as the National Socialists had used towards Jews, Gypsies etc. (a letter that I also never mailed and in fact tore into tiny shreds because I was feeling very ashamed and angry at myself, but yes, the novel did majorly rub me the wrong way, or rather, I should say that certain parts of <u>Starring Sally J. Freedman as Herself</u> majorly rubbed me the wrong way, totally upset and angered eleven year old me, and made me feel very small, insignificant and perhaps even deserving of being bullied because of my German culture and background).<br /><br />And thus, when I was reading (or rather when I was attempting to peruse) <u>Starring Sally J. Freedman as Herself</u> in grade five, I was most definitely focusing mainly on how Sally reacts (or rather how she so often strangely overreacts), and personally felt only absolute and utter sympathy for poor Mr. Zavodsky (and the unfounded, nasty and just plain silly accusations being cast at him) as well as rather intense (albeit also guilt-laden) anger at Sally, at her antics and attitudes (and yes, I absolutely did realise even then and totally understood the time and place, that Sally's aunt Rose and Rose's daughter Lila had been victims of the Holocaust, but that factoid did not and does NOT make me as a German automatically a potential Nazi and it does also NOT make Mr. Zavodsky automatically Hitler in disguise, even if he might have somewhat physically resembled him and spoken with a German accent). Furthermore, from the scenes at the beginning of <u>Starring Sally J. Freedman as Herself</u> (where Sally and her friends are often playacting WWII), I was forced to conclude (and perhaps even knew rather instinctively) that if I had been a member of Sally's group of friends, I probably would have (that is if Sally had even wanted a person of German background for a friend) ALWAYS been forced to assume the role of Adolf Hitler (or some other "evil" German character and that any and all refusal or argument on my part would more than likely have lead to at best a myriad of accusations).<br /><br />And finally, while this (and most definitely it will be my one and only) reread of <u>Starring Sally J. Freedman as Herself</u> has indeed made me a bit more appreciative of the fact that Judy Blume has been open with regard to her autobiography and that she has not shied away from depicting how truly nasty Sally often is towards Mr. Zadovsky (how she uses her overactive imagination to basically accuse him of being not only a potential National Socialist, but Adolf Hitler himself), I have still found <u>Starring Sally J. Freedman as Herself</u> a very much and truly in many ways trying and painfully saddening reading experience (even for me as an older adult), bringing to me as flashbacks ALL of the personal discomfort, sadness and anger I experienced in 1977 (when I was reading <u>Starring Sally J. Freedman as Herself</u> as an eleven year old recent German immigrant to Canada) and also strongly reminding me of the near constant bullying I was experiencing at that time from many of my "classmates" and some of my teachers simply because I just happened to be German.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13585508412416253569" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2128601240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11538825935356659034">What a strange book! From old ladies who look like Adolph Hitler to experiencing WWII from the safety of Florida, <i>Starring Sally J. Freedman As Herself</i> is a wonderful but complicated coming-of-age tale.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer29738107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2563061837519586960"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/1107842-my-goodreads-2019-summer-reading-challenge-list' rel='nofollow noopener'>Goodreads 2019 Summer Reading Challenge</a><br/>11. Past love: Reread a book you loved when you were younger<br/><br/>I have the distinct memory of this being my second least favorite Judy Blume book when I was a kid in the 1970s, and re-reading it again as an adult this week reminded me why -- because this is Blume's one and only historically autobiographical novel, set in the 1940s and concerning a Jewish girl in New Jersey whose family temporarily moves to Miami to help her brother recover from a kidney infecti</span>
  <span id="freeText2563061837519586960" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/1107842-my-goodreads-2019-summer-reading-challenge-list" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads 2019 Summer Reading Challenge</a><br />11. Past love: Reread a book you loved when you were younger<br /><br />I have the distinct memory of this being my second least favorite Judy Blume book when I was a kid in the 1970s, and re-reading it again as an adult this week reminded me why -- because this is Blume's one and only historically autobiographical novel, set in the 1940s and concerning a Jewish girl in New Jersey whose family temporarily moves to Miami to help her brother recover from a kidney infection, such a huge disconnect from my own life at ten that I found it almost impossible to engage with it. As an adult I was actually quietly charmed by all the hopelessly dated references Blume fondly looks back on here (the protagonist's love of Esther Williams; her insistence that Hitler escaped at the end of World War Two and is now living disguised in her apartment building; the family's habit of preparing cow's tongue for dinners; confusion over why "colored people" need their own drinking fountains, etc); but all this was simply too much for me to deal with when I was a kid myself, a book I was never able to get fully into and a problem that your own kids might have too. Recommended for Blume completists; but if you're just dipping your toes into her work for the first time, you're better off with an undisputed classic like <i>Are You There God? It's Me, Margaret</i>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2563061837519586960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_227088298" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227088298" />
    <a title="Alyssa Nelson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4665768-alyssa-nelson"><img alt="Alyssa Nelson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1397027844p2/4665768.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227088298?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa Nelson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa Nelson" href="/user/show/4665768-alyssa-nelson">Alyssa Nelson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4665768-alyssa-nelson?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4665768-alyssa-nelson?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227088298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5062244397069147136">I love Judy Blume for writing these wonderful books where the whole plot is just growing up and living life. This book is about Sally Freedman, a ten-year-old Jewish girl who is growing up just after the end of World War II; she moves to Florida with her mom and brother for her brother’s health and misses New York and her father a lot.<br/><br/>Blume has said that this is her most autobiographical work, and it shows in its full-colored, multi-layered portrayal of Sally’s life at ten years old. Sally is ju</span>
  <span id="freeText5062244397069147136" style="display:none">I love Judy Blume for writing these wonderful books where the whole plot is just growing up and living life. This book is about Sally Freedman, a ten-year-old Jewish girl who is growing up just after the end of World War II; she moves to Florida with her mom and brother for her brother’s health and misses New York and her father a lot.<br /><br />Blume has said that this is her most autobiographical work, and it shows in its full-colored, multi-layered portrayal of Sally’s life at ten years old. Sally is just in that stage where she’s starting to learn about some of life’s complexities, but she doesn’t quite understand everything perfectly and it is charming and heartwearming to read about her adventures and dreams. I especially loved how crushes and romance are handled in this story–at once sweet and hilarious.<br /><br />Friendships are also handled wonderfully in this. Sally has to struggle with keeping in touch with old friends in New York, but also fitting in with her new school and trying to make new friends. It’s so relatable and reading it as an adult, I got a lot of nostalgia/enjoyment out of reading about the squabbles that turn into end-of-the-world, friendship-ending dramas. It’s all just so relatable.<br /><br />This is a wonderful, fast, light read that is pure Judy Blume goodness.<br /><br />Also posted on <a href="https://www.purplereaders.com/?p=6244" rel="nofollow noopener">Purple People Readers</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5062244397069147136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7584128910947661665">Sally J. Freedman is a 12-13 year old girl who can best be described as having a creative imagination that runs wild! The book is set in the late 1940s. Sally and her mother and brother move to Florida for the winter, and Sally has managed to convince herself that an elderly man who lives in her apartment building is actually Adolf Hitler in disguise and he has come to Florida to retire.</span>

<div id="review_138827710" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/138827710" />
    <a title="Travis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4761577-travis"><img alt="Travis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507859363p2/4761577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/138827710?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Travis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Travis" href="/user/show/4761577-travis">Travis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4761577-travis?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4761577-travis?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4761577-travis?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138827710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer671011961004082781">I was recently reminded of this after a conversation about the rarity of children's books about Jews that aren't all Holocaust all the time. I remembered loving this as a kid and am pleased that it stands up well to a rereading as an adult. Blume really is a good writer.[return][return]This is the story of Sally, a ten-year-old girl who moves from New Jersey to Florida with her mom, brother, and grandma after World War II, because her brother has been ill and winters down south are recommended f</span>
  <span id="freeText671011961004082781" style="display:none">I was recently reminded of this after a conversation about the rarity of children's books about Jews that aren't all Holocaust all the time. I remembered loving this as a kid and am pleased that it stands up well to a rereading as an adult. Blume really is a good writer.[return][return]This is the story of Sally, a ten-year-old girl who moves from New Jersey to Florida with her mom, brother, and grandma after World War II, because her brother has been ill and winters down south are recommended for people's health. The community they move to seems to be all Jewish and most of the other families are also down there for the winter due to illness.[return][return]Not only does Sally have to make new friends, but she also has to adjust to how different things are in the south, such as calling everyone ma'am and sir, and segregation (I love when she writes to her dad, confused about someone who scolded her and her friend for using the colored water fountain, and her dad says it's not that different up north, people are just quieter about it, and as an example asks her how many black kids were in her old school in New Jersey).[return][return]The other main thread is Sally's wild imagination (including her deciding a strange old man who lives in their apartment building is Hitler in disguise) and how she misunderstands things she hears grown-ups talking about (reading this as an adult, it's much more amusing to see the things that fly over Sally's head).[return][return]If you never read this as a kid, or even if you did, I highly recommend checking it out. It's definitely a fun (and very quick) read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="671011961004082781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14883945310262990270">I have read this book countless times. It is the kind of book I pick up in between books. It is about a girl after World War II who moves to Florida for the winter. I really like this book because the main character makes a lot of mistakes, but then learns from them. She has all kinds of adventures, like going to a new school, making up stories in her head, and dreaming about her favorite movie star. This book just makes you smile. I don’t know how else to put it. 🙂</span>

          </span>

And it wasn't in whatever sub-par dictionary I looked it up in. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6963542183223717780">This was one of my favorite books from when I was a child. I overidentified with Sally (I also had a tendency to make up more interesting realities than my own) and I thought she was just really smart and fun.<br/><br/>And now there are spoilers.<br/><br/>Here's what I remembered going in: set shortly after World War II; Sally is Jewish and has several fantasies about saving her relatives who died in a concentration camp and killing Hitler; her older brother gets sick--something to do with his kidneys---and her gra</span>
  <span id="freeText6963542183223717780" style="display:none">This was one of my favorite books from when I was a child. I overidentified with Sally (I also had a tendency to make up more interesting realities than my own) and I thought she was just really smart and fun.<br /><br />And now there are spoilers.<br /><br />Here's what I remembered going in: set shortly after World War II; Sally is Jewish and has several fantasies about saving her relatives who died in a concentration camp and killing Hitler; her older brother gets sick--something to do with his kidneys---and her grandma is called "Ma Fanny."<br /><br />I have no idea how I managed to forget that Sally is convinced that one of her neighbors is Hitler living in disguise as a Jewish person. She actually writes him a bunch of letters telling him she knows who he is and she's going to find proof. She never mails any of them (she also doesn't mail the letters she writes to the police to tell them about her Hitler-neighbor) and thank goodness because can you imagine the reaction? This poor old Jewish man who has been mistaken for Hitler?<br /><br />Oh, Sally. I want to give you a hug and shake you at the same time.<br /><br />I love this book just as much as I did as a kid, though.<br /><br />Highly recommended.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2682116839" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15963136788388135306">This book was fine. It was a bit hard for me to get into initially, and so I had to start over a few times, but overall it was an okay book.<br/><br/>The summary made it seem like something bad was going to happen to Sally or someone in her family. Nothing much beyond life happened to them: just Sally and her brother Douglas growing up, and her mom worried over Sally's dad, because apparently his brothers both died when they were 42, and he was nearing 42. <br/><br/>One thing I thought was mildly interesting was th</span>
  <span id="freeText15963136788388135306" style="display:none">This book was fine. It was a bit hard for me to get into initially, and so I had to start over a few times, but overall it was an okay book.<br /><br />The summary made it seem like something bad was going to happen to Sally or someone in her family. Nothing much beyond life happened to them: just Sally and her brother Douglas growing up, and her mom worried over Sally's dad, because apparently his brothers both died when they were 42, and he was nearing 42. <br /><br />One thing I thought was mildly interesting was that since Sally was so young (and the fact that the book took place in 1947-48), there wasn't a lot about anything that she knew. There was actually a line in the book where Ma Fanny (that's what Sally calls her grandma) tells her and Douglas to eat their carrots because it'll help them see in the dark. That was wack. Also towards the end of the book Sally mentioned how her dad thinks that television is going to be the next big thing, but her mom thinks radio is going to stay forever. <br />Both are true, kinda. At this rate our technology has progressed past what people then could probably even imagine. <br /><br />I dunno, all in all the book was fine. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15963136788388135306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <a title="PinkAmy loves books, cats and naps " class="user" itemprop="url" name="PinkAmy loves books, cats and naps " href="/user/show/8149327-pinkamy-loves-books-cats-and-naps">PinkAmy loves books, cats and naps </a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1305448455" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10664877610219779514">Grade C<br/><br/>Although World War II has just ended, ten-year-old Sally is still preoccupied with Hitler. She writes stories about her cousin, who died in his camps, and even thinks her new neighbor just might be Hitler in disguise.<br/><br/>I loved bright, inquisitive Sally and all her creativity. I too wrote stories of peril when I was her age. STARRING SALLY J FREEDMAN AS HERSELF is a slice of life, period piece, one of Judy Blume's earliest and most autobiographical novel. As an adult, I enjoyed the story, bu</span>
  <span id="freeText10664877610219779514" style="display:none">Grade C<br /><br />Although World War II has just ended, ten-year-old Sally is still preoccupied with Hitler. She writes stories about her cousin, who died in his camps, and even thinks her new neighbor just might be Hitler in disguise.<br /><br />I loved bright, inquisitive Sally and all her creativity. I too wrote stories of peril when I was her age. STARRING SALLY J FREEDMAN AS HERSELF is a slice of life, period piece, one of Judy Blume's earliest and most autobiographical novel. As an adult, I enjoyed the story, but I have a hard time seeing most kids enjoying this story, because almost nothing happens. Today's kids seem more interested in books with more tension and action. Even Sally's dynamic personality can't make make up for a nonexistent plot. <br /><br />Sally's age probably means the YA crowd won't be drawn to STARRING SALLY J FREEDMAN AS HERSELF, which is too bad because a discussion of post WWII America for Jewish families would dovetail nicely into history lessons. I wish Blume had delved into some of the antisemitism any Jewish people experienced as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10664877610219779514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1886227446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17980148810279441234">I loved this book as a child, and decided to comfort-read it this week. I picked up a copy at Salvation army for fifty cents a couple years ago, and it has been sitting on my shelf ever since. I always thought that the book was about Hawaii, but it's actually set in Miami. ;)<br/><br/>I like the way Blume writes and the way that she deals with hard topics in a children's/teen book. Relationships, sex, breasts, babies, death and Hitler are all mentioned in this book. This book is set in 1947, but in many w</span>
  <span id="freeText17980148810279441234" style="display:none">I loved this book as a child, and decided to comfort-read it this week. I picked up a copy at Salvation army for fifty cents a couple years ago, and it has been sitting on my shelf ever since. I always thought that the book was about Hawaii, but it's actually set in Miami. ;)<br /><br />I like the way Blume writes and the way that she deals with hard topics in a children's/teen book. Relationships, sex, breasts, babies, death and Hitler are all mentioned in this book. This book is set in 1947, but in many ways, it's fairly progressive and feminist. But what I forgot about this book is how weird it actually is. Not much happens. There's one subplot where Sally becomes convinced that an old man living in her building is Hitler in disguise. <br /><br />I can also credit this book with part of my love for old movie stars, because Sally's love for Esther Williams made me curious about old movie stars when I initially read this book as a kid. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17980148810279441234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7601350308901223819">First sentence: "Can I have another jelly sandwich?" <div id="review_1622157977" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1622157977" />
    <a title="Jerry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5855981-jerry"><img alt="Jerry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520438201p2/5855981.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1622157977?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jerry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jerry" href="/user/show/5855981-jerry">Jerry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1622157977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3373006237499364322">It's been years since I've read any books by Judy Blume, and even longer since I've read anything of hers outside of the <i>Fudge</i> series. I'd heard that some of her other books caused controversy, and, with this one, it's not hard to see why. Suggestive content aside, the good writing in this book was marred by a boring story and too many disparaging remarks about God. Readers of youth-oriented fiction can do much better.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2457752555" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2457752555" />
    <a title="Ruth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/316631-ruth"><img alt="Ruth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1204062236p2/316631.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2457752555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16981066335738100076">I love Sally. My favorite thing about this book is the way it evokes all those years of trying to figure out the adult world as a kid- you get all these little snippets of conversation or things you see, and you're constantly trying to put them together to make sense of things, or to test them out yourself. In some ways I guess we do that forever, but when you're a kid it's almost like every conversation and every action is an experiment.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2868250498" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2868250498" />
    <a title="Kris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/802795-kris"><img alt="Kris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545888655p2/802795.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2868250498?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kris" href="/user/show/802795-kris">Kris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2868250498" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14517447665482880274">Even though this wasn't one of my favorite Judy Blume books as a kid, I still read it numerous times. I always liked that it was technically historical fiction, but it didn't feel like it. It just felt like another contemporary Judy Blume book that happened to be set right after World War II. That being said, Sally was never my favorite character. I liked her imagination, but I don't know that I actually liked her. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2419858280" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6532481280426546284">I enjoyed the plot, but I felt a bit lost. I feel it was fast-paced. Like, they would be at home, then suddenly in a blimp. I did, however, like Sally's imagination and how she would make stories.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8KxmyYi4SURxxJxNUcg5+7h39YCktStja4sPYw8U5QQJT8xHlsFsSEuvX2QNs2tYoc30mLYHlZdoK/TblJfB2w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/12942.Judy_Blume">About Judy Blume</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/12942.Judy_Blume"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1430843076p3/12942.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/12942.Judy_Blume">Judy Blume
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
8,718
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4772777185322429587">Judy Blume spent her childhood in Elizabeth, New Jersey, making up stories inside her head. She has spent her adult years in many places doing the same thing, only now she writes her stories down on paper. Adults as well as children will recognize such Blume titles as: Are You There God? It's Me, Margaret; Blubber; Just as Long as We're Together; and the five book series about the irrepressible Fu</span>
  <span id="freeText4772777185322429587" style="display:none">Judy Blume spent her childhood in Elizabeth, New Jersey, making up stories inside her head. She has spent her adult years in many places doing the same thing, only now she writes her stories down on paper. Adults as well as children will recognize such Blume titles as: Are You There God? It's Me, Margaret; Blubber; Just as Long as We're Together; and the five book series about the irrepressible Fudge. She has also written three novels for adults, Summer Sisters; Smart Women; and Wifey, all of them New York Times bestsellers. More than 80 million copies of her books have been sold, and her work has been translated into thirty-one languages. She receives thousands of letters a year from readers of all ages who share their feelings and concerns with her.<br />Judy received a B.S. in education from New York University in 1961, which named her a Distinguished Alumna in 1996, the same year the American Library Association honored her with the Margaret A. Edwards Award for Lifetime Achievement. Other recognitions include the Library of Congress Living Legends Award and the 2004 National Book Foundation's Medal for Distinguished Contribution to American Letters.<br />She is the founder and trustee of The Kids Fund, a charitable and educational foundation. She serves on the boards of the Author's Guild; the Society of Children's Book Writers and Illustrators; the Key West Literary Seminar; and the National Coalition Against Censorship.<br />Judy is a longtime advocate of intellectual freedom. Finding herself at the center of an organized book banning campaign in the 1980's she began to reach out to other writers, as well as teachers and librarians, who were under fire. Since then, she has worked tirelessly with the National Coalition Against Censorship to protect the freedom to read. She is the editor of Places I Never Meant To Be, Original Stories by Censored Writers.<br />Judy has completed a series of four chapter books -- The Pain &amp; the Great One -- illustrated by New Yorker cartoonist James Stevenson. She has co-written and produced a film adaptation of her book Tiger Eyes, and is currently writing a new novel.<br />Judy and her husband George Cooper live on islands up and down the east coast. They have three grown children and one grandchild.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4772777185322429587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
